## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration in such systems typically includes restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t). Classical nonlinear oscillator models include Duffing, Van der Pol, and driven oscillators.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Linear damping + restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (damped Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (periodically driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Driven harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven damped linear oscillator)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Quadratic-cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear potential)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v (nonlinear friction depending on position)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Softening spring with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5) (general driven Duffing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells, preserving oscillatory symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → linear energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Terms like (1 - c*x**2)*v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillators (Van der Pol type)
- Cubic position term x**3 → hardening (same sign as linear term) or softening (opposite sign) spring behavior
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force
- Even powers of x (x**2) in restoring force → broken symmetry / asymmetric oscillation about equilibrium
- Products x**n * v → nonlinear coupling between position-dependent stiffness and velocity (parametric effects)
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence indicates external forcing

**GT:** `-1.1449635767559*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.445567501246416*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.10853689295113*sin(t)`

The GT has three basis functions:
1. `x*exp(-|x|)` — a product of x and exp(-|x|)
2. `log(|v| + 1)` — logarithm of (|v| + 1); since v ≤ 0 on this domain, |v| = -v
3. `sin(t)` — simple sine of t

Key observations:
- The `x*exp(-|x|)` term is highly nonlinear and cannot be represented by polynomials, rational functions of x, or simple exponentials of x.
- The `log(|v|+1)` term is logarithmic in v and cannot be represented by linear functions of v, exp(v), or polynomial functions of v.
- Most candidates use rational functions in x like `x/(c*x²+1)` or polynomial terms in x.

Let me check if `x/(c*x²+1)` could equal `x*exp(-|x|)`. No — these are fundamentally different functions. `x*exp(-|x|)` decays exponentially while `x/(cx²+1)` decays as 1/x. They cannot be equal for all x.

Similarly, `exp(c*x)` cannot match `exp(-|x|)` because |x| is not linear in x.

Let me check candidates that might have both `exp(-|x|)` (or equivalent) and `log(|v|+1)`:

Going through all candidates systematically:

- **Candidate 58**: Has `exp(c1*x)` — this is `exp(cx)` which cannot equal `exp(-|x|)` for all x (both positive and negative). **NO MATCH**.
